text:
OMG, this is AMAZING!  We loved it!  After reading the reviews I added some things.  I added 1/4 cup of white wine (Chardonnay) when I added the lemon juice, I used 2 tbs of lemon juice instead of 1, a couple more cloves of fresh garlic, and I sauted red and yellow pepper, mushrooms, and red onions and added them in with the chicken.  I also added the pasta in with the chicken at the end so it could get all the great flavor!  My husband kept saying this tastes like restaurant quality and it really did!  It's really fresh tasting and you can taste every ingredient. It wasn't too greasy either.  It would be great to serve for company and it's super easy too!  Thanks for the great Italian recipe!

text:
This recipe is INCREDIBLE. It is most definitely the base for creating an authentic Olive Garden-style Chicken Scampi. I used chicken tenderloins instead of sliced breasts and coated them in flour before cooking them. A also added extra garlic, since I'm a garlic lover. When the chicken was almost done cooking I added red onion and red, yellow, and green bell pepper cut into strips. Serve over angel hair pasta and and top with grated Parmesan cheese and I don't think anyone could tell the difference between this and the restaurant original! The only thing I recommend is keeping the heat down to medium - the chicken will cook slower but the garlic won't get burned - burned garlic will utterly ruin the whole meal with its bitter taste. Thank-you, thank-you, thank-you Cyndee for this wonderful recipe!!

text:
What a great recipe!  I ended up serving it over angle hair pasta and it worked out perfectly for two... you may want to consider doubling the recipe if you're thinking about serving more people than I did.  Otherwise, I added about a half cup of white wine to the sauce while the chicken was cooking and cut up a tomato for some more color.  I cooked the chicken on low heat and would suggest doing so if any of you try this.  Too high and you'll sear it (trap the juices inside) and prevent it from flavoring the sauce... which it does beautifully!  Also, I parboiled some broccoli, sauteed it in garlic, and added it right before I served everything -- turned out so well!!!  Top it with parmasean cheese for the finishing touch :)

Very good! I carefully read through a great amount of reviews and followed some good suggestions - 1/2 the butter in the recipe, use only 2 Tlbs. of Olive oil, more garlic (I used 4 big cloves), added 1/2 cup of white wine, 1 diced tomato for color, added a small red chili pepper chopped fine and last but not least topped it with fresh grated parmasan cheese. It came out perfect!

text:
Delicious!!  One of the cooks at my Dad's restaurant used to make this for me every day  when I was a kid.  Being very picky, it was one of the few things they could get me to eat.  I've ordered chicken scampi in rest. a number of times in hopes that it would be the dish I ate as a kid.  No luck....until now!! I will make this again and again.  Perhaps try adding a little white wine sometime, maybe a little more lemon and a little less salt.  But it's great as is. I actually like the large amount of butter and olive oil sauce it yeilds as it is great over pasta.  Be sure to have some fresh Parmesan to grate over the top when serving.  Goes great over angel hair and makes awesome leftovers.

text:
This was delicious!  I did cut out a lot of fat and calories by browning the chicken and spices in only 1/4 cup butter, then added 1/2 cup of chicken broth and let the chicken simmer until done, then added some cornstarch to thicken it up just a little.  Served over angel hair pasta with salad and french bread.  It was a wonderful, fairly low fat meal.  I will be making this one again!

I was surprised at how good this dish was. It was also a cinch to prepare. I didn't measure a thing, I just added as much as I like. I used fresh basil and fresh parsley from my herb garden, that made a huge difference. Also, I tossed the cooked pasta in the dish I made the sauce in to make sure it coated well. I don't recommend cooking the chicken for 10-15 minutes, check it after 5. This dish was good enough to make for company. Thanks for sharing. I've had this recipe for years now and am glad I finally tried it!

text:
This is the first review I've written after using this site for about 5 years and making dozens of recipes - just to give an idea of how good this recipe is.  I read the reviews and used some of their suggestions: did not turn the heat up too high to avoid burning the garlic, dredged the chicken in flour, used half of the butter to start with and the remaining half throughout while cooking.  I also used about 1/4 cup of white wine when putting in the lemon juice and used about 4 cloves of garlic.  Once the chicken is cooked, I added chopped yellow and red bell peppers (1/2 of each), mushrooms and fresh broccoli.  After letting it cook for another minute or two, I added my cooked angel hair pasta and tossed it all together in the pan.  DELICIOUS!  My two sons and husband ate it all up and barely even talked.  VERY, VERY good recipe.

text:
I could have died happy the night I made this dish. I made it Olive Garden style by pounding the chicken flat then dredging it in flour before cooking, then I added thinly sliced red and green bell pepers and red onion. Dredging the chicken is an absolute necessity!!!! But make sure and shake off as much excess flour as possible. You'll be glad you add this step, especially if you've ever had the chicken scampi at Olive Garden.

Yummy! I doubled the lemon juice which was terrific. I halved the butter and oil but I would have liked more sauce so next time maybe i'll add some chicken broth to the sauce.  I used 4 large garlic cloves and it was garlicy but good.  I also cut the chicken in chunks to get more surface area to soak up the sauce. OKAY- I made this again adding 1/2 can of chicken broth after I sauteed the chicken.  Definitely gave it more sauce but not as good.  Maybe I'll try to use 1/4 can next time. We thought this was just terrific!  And, I gave it 5 stars due to how easy it was.  If it was harder, I may have given it a four, but taking everything into consideration (time, taste, presentation, etc.), it's a 5 for a weeknight meal.  I did cut the butter to 1/4 cup (and then needed a tad more b/c I had so much chicken).  I also added a couple splashes of extra lemon juice, which definitely helped. I could have probably added more garlic, but I really love garlic, soooo that may just be an issue of personal taste.  I served it over spaghetti noodles -- don't forget to leave your noodles unrinsed so the sauce sticks!  My husband loved this!

4.5 stars!  This was really good, really fast and really easy!  I happened to have all the ingredients on hand, which is always nice.  I used extra virgin olive oil, which gave it a really nice flavor.  I also added the lemon juice to the pan before the butter and oil became hot, as I was leary of adding liquid to a pan of hot oil.  I sauted the chicken for 5 minutes per side and did not touch them other than to flip them.  They get a nice golden brown this way.  I served it over whole wheat spaghetti.  I think this would be even better if it were marinated in the lemon juice and herbs overnight with a touch of white wine and red pepper flakes added.  Next time I plan to tweak it to be more like the dish at Olive Garden.

text:
A quick and easy scampi that was quite delicious. I took the advice of others and cut the oil and butter in half as well as adding some wine with the lemon juice. (Only had fortified wines handy, so I used Marsala...just a few tablespoons.) I did do one thing entirely different, though, with great results. Recalling the French technique of monter au buerre, I began the dish with 2 tablespoons of butter, then, after the chicken was cooked through (which i found easier if the pan was lidded) I removed it from the pan, put a splash of my pasta cooking water in the pan to increase the volume of liquid, and whisked in the other two tablespoons of cold butter, about a teaspoon at a time. This results in a creamy, silky finish to the sauce.

text:
Oh YUMM!! What a delicious and simple dish! I especially enjoyed this recipe as i keep a kosher home and it's often times hard to find such a yummy recipe without having to make too many changes and keep it kosher. Like many others, i took the time a read through all the comments, and tweaked the recipe slightly.  Used 5-6 large garlic cloves, I halved the margarine(but then added addtl. 1 Tbs) & 1tsp of Wondra(to thicken a bit) during the last couple minutes of simmering.  In addition, i added 1/4cup of chardonnay at the same time i added the lemon juice, which i also doubled to 2 Tbs.  Also, after the initial sauteing of the chicken was done, i added 1 plum tomato(halved, seeded, sliced length wise), 1/2 of one red onion, sliced thinly, length wise) and 1/2 bag of fresh spinach during the last five mins. of cooking.  The only other change i made was the chicken itself, i cut each breast into smaller strips instead of just thirding them.  It was a wonderful dish, and my fiance gave it 2 thumbs up and said he'd be happy to eat it again anytime!!

text:
This was awesome!! I did make some modifications, to make it healthier. I cut the olive oil down to 2 tbs., used "I Can't Believe It's Not Butter" spray in place of the real thing. I made up the difference in liquid with chicken broth. I am a garlic lover, so I used 5 cloves. I used 2 chicken breasts, and cut them into 'tender' size strips as others had suggested. After sauteing the chicken, I added chopped mushrooms, zucchini, and sun-dried tomatoes. About 5 minutes before serving, I tossed in Mueller's whole grain pasta and chopped artichoke hearts. This was a wonderful meal! I think I will try it using vegetables only and serve as a side dish-would be great with grilled fish. This is definitely a keeper. Thanks Cyndee!

Simply awesome, it's a nice recipe that you can adapt to what you have on hand. Instead of the suggested herbs I used Italian Seasoning Blend and a handful of fresh chopped parsley. Reading a pile of reviews I followed several suggestions. Cooking for two, we have basil and oregano in our garden and chives and used out of the garden fresh, a little labor intense! Hands down one of the best chicken scampi dishes I ever had.  I added about 1 1/2 cup of white cooking wine and put it over angel hair pasta and cooked (or steamed) broccoli.

One trick for extremely moist chicken... after you saute the chicken, shut the flame off, cover, and let sit for an hour or two.  The chicken absorbs all the flavors as well.  Reheat it before serving.

text:
I was looking for a way to salvage some chicken breasts from another recipe, which came out tasting like they had been poached. This worked well. In addition to all the listed ingredients, I used 1/2 cup white cooking wine, an extra tablespoon of lemon juice, and 1/2 cup of sun-dried tomatoes in oil (drained) - reduced it down by simmering for about 10 minutes, then added the cooked chicken breasts, which I had sliced into medallions. They cooked for about five minutes, turning them over half way through. Then I put them on plates and sprinkled feta cheese over them. Wow - this is absolutely delicious.

This was a fast and easy dinner and my family really enjoyed it. I did follow some of the other reviewers suggestions, I cut down on the butter and oil (3T butter, 1T oil) used more garlic (8 cloves) and added 1/2 cup white once the chicken was partially cooked. I put Parmesan on the table and let everyone add as much or as little as they wanted. My mom ended up having three helpings!

I made this using others' suggestions... I doubled the sauce (actually only used 3/4C of butter instead of 1) and used a 1/2 cup of white wine.  I also used fresh herbs instead of dried.  The sauce really was delicious... of course very rich, but delicious.  My problem had nothing to do flavor but more with the combination of that rich sauce and chicken.  The recipe SOUNDED like it would be really good but in reality the combination of the super-rich sauce and the chicken just didn't do it for me.  For lack of another word, the chicken seemed too HEAVY for such a rich sauce. For leftovers i'll use the sauce over pasta alone and probably cut the chicken up into a salad. Would be willing to try it with shrimp ... if I made it again I'd add more spices as well as it was a bit bland.  Maybe more salt/wine/lemon/basil.  Not more garlic!

text:
Simply delicious!  I have made this recipe several times as it is a big hit with my family.  Even the two-year-old eats every bite!  That's a good indicator of a great recipe!  I generally serve it over linguini noodles or penne, or sometimes even bowtie pasta for some fun for the kids.  I also accompany it with fresh sourdough bread to soak up the sauce.  Mmmm...so good!  The only thing you have to watch is not to scorch the sauce.  I have done this twice now (got distracted and let it get too hot) and it turned all the garlic dark brown and changed the overall taste a little.  It was still good, but definitely tastes better if you keep an eye on it and don't scorch it.  This recipe will continue to be one of my personal favorites for a long, long time.

text:
This recipe was very good...I did follow others suggestions and tweaked the recipe a bit and it was one of the best pasta dishes I've ever had!!!  I reduced the amount of butter and oil to about half of what it said.  I added 1/2 can of chicken broth (99% fat free) and about 1/4 cup or white wine (Chardonnay).  I substituted italian seasoning for basil and oregano.  I also seasoned the chicken with salt and pepper and added 1 whole chopped tomatos.  I simmered all of this at about medium to medium-low heat until the chicken was cooked through (about 20-30 mins) and tomatos were almost translucent.  I cooked the noodles and added right into the skillet with the chicken and the sauce.  I served with hawaiian rolls since I didn't have garlic bread on hand.  My husband LOVED it and had seconds and even thirds!!! :)  He sneaked into the kitchen with his rolls and mopped up the rest of the sauce in the skillet with his rolls!!

Out of all the recipes we've tried for scampi this is by far the best.  I already can't wait to make it again.  It is very falvorful, easy, and filling.  I actually just finished off the leftovers for lunch and it was just as good!  
Some additions:
Place 1/4 cup of water and one chicken bouillion cube in the microwave until disolved.  Add a 1/4 cup of Chardonnay (we use Cafe Chardonnay).  Add all of this to the saute when adding lemon juice.  Cook 2 cups of egg noodles and toss generously with the chicken scampi for each serving.
Excellent recipe!

I was craving shrimp scampi and came across this recipe. Very good. Reminds me a bit of the Olive Garden Chicken Scampi. I made this exactly as written except I lightly coated the chicken with flour and added some red and green peppers and a couple shakes of granulated garlic on top of the minced garlic. I thought it was good, but definitely needs some tweaking next time I make it. A lot less olive oil (it was pretty dominant over the other flavors), a lot more garlic (2-3x more), more salt and a lot more lemon. I'd like to try adding some white wine with it as well. Overall super easy to make, with ingredients I already had on hand. Good recipe that I will play around with.

text:
I thought the picture of the dish looked palely unappealing so I sauteed/browned the chicken in the butter/olive oil right at the start.  When it was cooked, I removed the chicken, then added the garlic and herbs to the pan, added 1/2 c. white wine along with the tablespoon of lemon juice, did a reduction to get all the good bits up off the pan.  I cooked some bowtie pasta (I had no linguine) and combined everything for a nice meal.  I used less salt and probably half the butter called for.  I'll likely make this again but I will cut the chicken in bite size pieces and salt it directly before cooking.

This was better than Olive Garden. I made this yesterday for 4th of July and everyone LOVED it. I doubled the recipe and got a huge bowl full of delicious Chicken Scampi. I too added the 1/2 cup white wine as well as sauted red onion, bell pepper, garlic and tomatoes. Instead of searing the chicken, I grilled it ahead of time and once the sauce was made, I put the sliced grilled chicken in and stirred it on low heat for about 3 minutes. Just enough for it to get flavor. I used wheat angel hair pasta and mixed everything together and then served. This was an amazing recipe. Thanks to everyone who suggested the tweaks! city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
Do you like a little chicken with your butter?  This recipe seemed to be crying out for a lower fat version.  One half cup of butter, plus the olive oil is way more than is needed.  I used one tablespoon of butter and one of olive oil and followed the recipe, except I did not add the garlic until after the chicken did its initial browning.  I then added the garlic and a half cup each of chicken stock and dry white wine and simmered the chicken (about 10-15 minutes) until it was cooked through.  (I used fairly large pieces.) To finish it off I thickened the sauce with two tablespoons of cornstarch mixed into a couple more tablespoons of chicken stock.  I served this over couscous (with diced onions and red pepper).  While my version probably does not match the buttery blast of the original recipe it may be easier on the arteries.

text:
This is a great recipe.  I have made this quite a few times.  The differences I make are more for our own personal preferences and we like it better than the original, but we do add a green and red bell pepper diced, a can of corn, white wine - about a 1/2 cup and at the end, we toss in some parm cheese.  I think the recipe is an excellent starter one that you can tweak very easily to your own liking.  I also like to add in some red pepper flakes and some additional lemon juice.  I end up heating up the oil and butter together with a diced onion garlic, tossing in the chicken breasts that I diced up, then a few minutes later add in all of the veggies, herbs/spices, lemon juice and white wine.  I let it simmer for about 15-20 minutes while I get the pasta ready.  When the pasta is ready, dump in the chicken mixture, toss in some parm cheese and serve.  I highly recommend this to anyone!

text:
This has to be the most-reviewed recipe I've made yet. I usually read all the previous reviews before posting mine, but this time I'll pass on reading all 427 of them.
I had a mixed experience with this recipe. I made it exactly as written (the olive oil I used was "extra virgin", by the way). When cooking it, I was excited because it sure looked and smelled like a real "shrimp scampi" with chicken instead of shrimp. But when I ate it (for two dinners, on a bed of white rice), it just seemed "okay". The chicken breast halves I used were very large, and therefore the "thirds" were also big. I think smaller chicken strips would have been a lot better. And I would have liked a lot more garlic flavor to the sauce. I'll still give this a 4-star review since my suggested changes are kind of minor.

Have made this twice now, two different ways.  The first time, I made according to the directions with a few changes (half the butter, extra garlic, and white wine).  My boyfriend loved it, and said I could make it again.  The second time I didn't use the stove.  My grandmother poached the chicken in the oven, and I made the sauce in the microwave.  Only change I made was to add extra garlic.  Put everything but the lemon juice in the microwave for a couple of minutes, stirring every 30 seconds or so.  The family enjoyed it, and asked me to make it again.  Easy recipe that is easily modified.

My only complaint is that when mixed with the pasta (and I didn't use that much), the dish lost a lot of flavor.  We doused it with parm, which is always a savior.  However, next time I will use more butter and possibly marinate the chicken in the herbs and garlic before cooking it.  Overall, it's a good recipe.  I'm a huge fan of it at the O.Garden, and this is close.
